 The secondary gamma-ray spectrum for radiative capture (MF 12,    725 1451   20
 MT 102) has been updated for new experimental data at incident    725 1451   21
 neutron energies up to 400 keV. The Q-value for radiative capture 725 1451   22
 was also updated in File 3.  Details of these changes are         725 1451   23
 described in Frankle et al. [Fr01].                               725 1451   24

****************************************************************** 725 1451   29
                                                                   725 1451   30
 ENDF/B-VI MOD 4 Evaluation, August 1997, M.B. Chadwick and        725 1451   31
           P.G. Young (LANL)                                       725 1451   32
                                                                   725 1451   33
 Los Alamos LA150 Library, produced with FKK/GNASH/GSCAN code      725 1451   34
   in cooperation with ECN Petten.                                 725 1451   35
                                                                   725 1451   36
   This evaluation provides a complete representation of the       725 1451   37
 nuclear data needed for transport, damage, heating,               725 1451   38
 radioactivity, and shielding applications over the incident       725 1451   39
 neutron energy range from 1.0E-11 to 150 MeV.  The discussion     725 1451   40
 here is divided into the region below and above 20 MeV.           725 1451   41
                                                                   725 1451   42
 INCIDENT NEUTRON ENERGIES < 20 MeV                                725 1451   43
   Below 20 MeV the evaluation is based completely on the ENDF/B-  725 1451   44
 VI.3 (Release 3) evaluation by P. G. Young, G. M. Hale, and M.    725 1451   45
 B. Chadwick [Yo94].                                               725 1451   46
                                                                   725 1451   47
 INCIDENT NEUTRON ENERGIES > 20 MeV                                725 1451   48
   The ENDF/B-VI Release 3 evaluation of n + 14N data extends to   725 1451   49
 40 MeV and includes cross sections and energy-angle data for all  725 1451   50
 significant reactions.  The present evaluation utilizes a more    725 1451   51
 compact composite reaction spectrum representation of the data    725 1451   52
 above 20 MeV in order to reduce the length of the file, and we    725 1451   53
 have only included the ENDF/B-VI data below 20 MeV. To avoid      725 1451   54
 redundancy, the sections MT=78-90 are removed, since their        725 1451   55
 thresholds lie between 20 and 40 MeV. No essential data for       725 1451   56
 applications is lost with our representation above 20 MeV.        725 1451   57
   The evaluation above 20 MeV utilizes MF=6, MT=5 to represent    725 1451   58
 all reaction data.  Production cross sections and emission        725 1451   59
 spectra are given for neutrons, protons, deuterons, tritons,      725 1451   60
 alpha particles, gamma rays, and all residual nuclides produced   725 1451   61
 (A>5) in the reaction chains. To summarize, the ENDF sections     725 1451   62
 with non-zero data above En = 20 MeV are:                         725 1451   63
                                                                   725 1451   64
  MF=3 MT=  1  Total Cross Section                                 725 1451   65
       MT=  2  Elastic Scattering Cross Section                    725 1451   66
       MT=  3  Nonelastic Cross Section                            725 1451   67
       MT=  5  Sum of Binary (n,n') and (n,x) Reactions            725 1451   68
                                                                   725 1451   69
  MF=4 MT=  2  Elastic Angular Distributions                       725 1451   70
                                                                   725 1451   71
  MF=6 MT=  5  Production Cross Sections and Energy-Angle          725 1451   72
               Distributions for Emission Neutrons, Protons,       725 1451   73
               Deuterons, Tritons, and Alphas; and Angle-          725 1451   74
               Integrated Spectra for Gamma Rays and Residual      725 1451   75
               Nuclei That Are Stable Against Particle Emission    725 1451   76
                                                                   725 1451   77
   The evaluation is based on nuclear model calculations that have 725 1451   78
 been benchmarked to experimental data, especially for n + 14N     725 1451   79
 and p + 14N reactions [Ch97]. We use the GNASH code system        725 1451   80
 [Yo92], which utilizes Hauser-Feshbach statistical,               725 1451   81
 preequilibrium and direct-reaction theories. Spherical optical    725 1451   82
 model calculations are used to obtain particle transmission       725 1451   83
 coefficients for the Hauser-Feshbach calculations, as well as     725 1451   84
 for the elastic neutron angular distributions.                    725 1451   85
   Cross sections and spectra for producing individual residual    725 1451   86
 nuclei are included for reactions. The energy-angle-correlations  725 1451   87
 for all outgoing particles are based on Kalbach systematics       725 1451   88
 [Ka88].                                                           725 1451   89
   A model was developed to calculate the energy distributions of  725 1451   90
 all recoil nuclei in the GNASH calculations [Ch96]. The recoil    725 1451   91
 energy distributions are represented in the laboratory system in  725 1451   92
 MT=5, MF=6, and are given as isotropic in the lab system. All     725 1451   93
 other data in MT=5,MF=6 are given in the center-of-mass system.   725 1451   94
 This method of representation utilizes the LCT=3 option approved  725 1451   95
 at the November, 1996, CSEWG meeting.                             725 1451   96
   Preequilibrium corrections were performed in the course of the  725 1451   97
 GNASH calculations using the exciton model of Kalbach [Ka77],     725 1451   98
 [Ka85], validated by comparison with calculations using Feshbach, 725 1451   99
 Kerman, Koonin (FKK) theory [Ch93].  Discrete level data from     725 1451  100
 nuclear data sheets were matched to continuum level densities     725 1451  101
 using the formulation of Ignatyuk [Ig75] and pairing and shell    725 1451  102
 parameters from the Cook [Co67] analysis. Neutron and charged-    725 1451  103
 particle transmission coefficients were obtained from the         725 1451  104
 optical potentials, as discussed below.  Gamma-ray transmission   725 1451  105
 coefficients were calculated using the Kopecky-Uhl model [Ko90].  725 1451  106
                                                                   725 1451  107
 DETAILS OF THE n + 14N ANALYSIS                                   725 1451  108
   GNASH calculations [Yo92,Ch94] were performed for neutron and   725 1451  109
 proton reactions on nitrogen up to 150 MeV, and the calculated    725 1451  110
 results were benchmarked against experimental data. For neutrons  725 1451  111
 below 100 MeV, the present evaluation made extensive use of our   725 1451  112
 previous work [Ch96a].  Very minor differences with this earlier  725 1451  113
 work exist due to recent developments in the GNASH code. Much use 725 1451  114
 was made of measured data in the evaluation, since an accurate    725 1451  115
 modeling of reactions on a light nucleus is difficult. In this    725 1451  116
 way we were able to obtain a fairly good description of the       725 1451  117
 emission spectra of secondary particles and gamma rays.           725 1451  118
 Additionally, the (angle-integrated) emission spectra of heavy    725 1451  119
 recoils were calculated using our model described in Ref. [Ch96]. 725 1451  120
 Some additional information on this evaluation can be found in    725 1451  121
 Ref. [Ch97].                                                      725 1451  122
   Between 20 and 150 MeV, the optical models used (the neutron    725 1451  123
 potential of Islam below 60 MeV [Is88]; Madland's potential       725 1451  124
 [Ma88] at higher energies, with Lane transformations for the      725 1451  125
 proton potential) provided a reasonably good description of       725 1451  126
 measured reaction cross section data. But since a very accurate   725 1451  127
 description of the reaction cross section is important for        725 1451  128
 determining secondary particle spectra, we slightly modify the    725 1451  129
 calculated results to better describe the experimental data, and  725 1451  130
 renormalize the calculated transmission coefficients accordingly. 725 1451  131
 The SCAT2 code [Be92] was used to calculate the transmission      725 1451  132
 coefficients. No measurements for the neutron reaction cross      725 1451  133
 section on nitrogen exist above about 50 MeV. However,            725 1451  134
 systematics have been determined from a number of target elements 725 1451  135
 at 95 MeV by DeJuren [De50], and for 100 MeV protons by Kirby and 725 1451  136
 Link [Ki66] (at this energy the proton and neutron reaction cross 725 1451  137
 sections would be expected to be very similar). We have,          725 1451  138
 therefore, used these systematics to guide our evaluated reaction 725 1451  139
 cross sections. Additionally, below 50 MeV we have also been      725 1451  140
 guided by the proton-induced reaction cross sections of Carlson   725 1451  141
 et al. [Ca75]. Experimental total elastic scattering values of    725 1451  142
 Islam et al. [Is88], Olsson et al. [Ol90], and Petler et al.      725 1451  143
 [Pe85] were obtained by subtracting their angle-integrated        725 1451  144
 elastic data from the evaluated total cross sections (see below). 725 1451  145
 The evaluated total cross section was obtained by slightly        725 1451  146
 modifying the optical model results to agree with data,           725 1451  147
 principally the new high-accuracy results of Finlay et al.        725 1451  148
 [Fi93]. We use the ENDF/B-VI total cross section below 40 MeV     725 1451  149
 recently evaluated by Young [Yo94].                               725 1451  150
   Preequilibrium spectra for incident energies below 100 MeV were 725 1451  151
 taken from our previous work [Ch96], where they were evaluated    725 1451  152
 from a combination of FKK calculations [Ch93], and measured       725 1451  153
 emission spectra data, while ensuring that unitarity is conserved 725 1451  154
 (i.e., making sure the sum of primary emitted preequilibrium      725 1451  155
 spectra does not exceed the reaction cross section). This         725 1451  156
 approach has the advantage of facilitating a good representation  725 1451  157
 of emission spectra experimental data. However, the lack of such  725 1451  158
 data above 100 MeV prohibits its extension to higher energies,    725 1451  159
 and therefore above 100 MeV, exciton model calculations were      725 1451  160
 utilized from the GNASH code [Ka77, Ka85]. This results in some   725 1451  161
 (small) discontinuities around 100 MeV in the production cross    725 1451  162
 sections, though the impact of this is negligible for most        725 1451  163
 applications.                                                     725 1451  164
   Nuclear level densities were determined using the Ignatyuk      725 1451  165
 model [Ig75], as implemented by Arthur et al. [Yo92].  Pairing    725 1451  166
 energies were obtained from the Cook systematics with the Los     725 1451  167
 Alamos extensions to light nuclei from [Ar83].  This continuum    725 1451  168
 level density formulation is matched continuously onto discrete   725 1451  169
 low-lying levels at the lower excitation energies. Discrete level 725 1451  170
 information (energy, spin, parity, gamma-ray branching ratios) is 725 1451  171
 tabulated for each nuclide in an input file, which is based on    725 1451  172
 the Ajzenberg-Selove compilations.  For each nucleus we performed 725 1451  173
 a level-density analysis and determined the excitation energy at  725 1451  174
 which we judged the level data complete. Gamma-ray transmission   725 1451  175
 coefficients were obtained from the Kopecky-Uhl model [Ko90].     725 1451  176
   An important test of the accuracy of the data libraries is that 725 1451  177
 the evaluated emission spectra of light particles (A < 5) should  725 1451  178
 be consistent with the measurements by Subramanian et al.  of UC- 725 1451  179
 Davis [Su86].  We have compared our calculated (lab frame) angle- 725 1451  180
 integrated emission spectra of protons, deuterons, and alphas,    725 1451  181
 with these measurements, with good agreement. The structure seen  725 1451  182
 at high emission energies is due to the inclusion of discrete     725 1451  183
 nuclear levels in our calculations. Also, kerma factors obtained  725 1451  184
 from the evaluated cross sections are in fairly good agreement    725 1451  185
 with experimental data [Ch96].                                    725 1451  186
                                                                   725 1451  187

 ENDF/B-VI MOD 3 Revision, August 1994, P.G. Young  (LANL)         725 1451  190
                                                                   725 1451  191
   This modification corrects the elastic and inelastic cross      725 1451  192
 sections (MT=63-90) at incident neutron energies above 13.5.MeV   725 1451  193
 given in MOD 2 of ENDF/B-VI.  This correction was made to         725 1451  194
 improve agreement with elastic scattering measurements up to      725 1451  195
 25 MeV.  The elastic neutron angular distributions above 20 MeV   725 1451  196
 were also improved over the earlier data distributed in MOD 2,    725 1451  197
 based upon fits to experimental data.                             725 1451  198

 ENDF/B-VI MOD 2 Evaluation, September 1992, P.G. Young (LANL)     725 1451  202
                                                                   725 1451  203
 Extension to 40 MeV                                               725 1451  204
     The modified version of the ENDF/B-VI evaluation created for  725 1451  205
 DNA (described below) is extended in energy to 40 MeV. This ext-  725 1451  206
 tension was accomplished using experimental data and the 9/92     725 1451  207
 Version of the GNASH code, which was updated for higher energy    725 1451  208
 calculations. More details will be given in a later progress      725 1451  209
 report.                                                           725 1451  210
     The ENDF/B-VI evaluation was modified for DNA use to include  725 1451  211
 results from Hale's R-matrix analysis that include Harvey's new   725 1451  212
 total cross section measurement. These results are interim until  725 1451  213
 we can incorporate the new ORNL scattering data. The ORNL         725 1451  214
 preliminary scattering results confirm the parity of the first    725 1451  215
 resonance as being positive, as used in the R-matrix analysis.    725 1451  216
                                                                   725 1451  217

GENERAL COMMENTS:                                                  725 1451  225
   The ENDF/B-VI data file for N14 is an essentially complete new  725 1451  226
evaluation. Below 2.5 MeV, it consists of an R-matrix analysis of  725 1451  227
the available experimental total, elastic, (n,p0), and (n,alpha0)  725 1451  228
cross sections and angular distributions using the EDA coupled-    725 1451  229
channel r-matrix code. At higher energies, the evaluation          725 1451  230
is an update of the 1972 evaluation of Young and Foster [Yo72]     725 1451  231
to include new experimental data since that time. More details     725 1451  232
of the evaluation are included below.                              725 1451  233
